MEMORANDUM
Date:          September 5, 2013                                                 TG:       12129.00
To:            Christina Fera-Thomas, City of Hillsboro
               Jinde Zhu, Washington County

               Scott Lee
cc:            Scott Franklin, PACLAND

Subject:       Sequoia Village TIA ­ Response to Comments

This memorandum provides additional information and clarifications in response to comments
received from the City of Hillsboro within the Determination of Application Status ­ Concept
Development Plan Case File No. Concept Development Plan 1-13: Sequoia Village. In addition,
additional information has been provided based on discussions with Washington County staff. A
summary of the requested information and responses to each are provided below.


City of Hillsboro Determination of Application Status:
Provide supporting documentation for queuing in the appendix (output from VISSIM).
The output summary for the VISSIM analysis has been provided in Attachment 1. Detailed outputs
have been provided by email to the City of Hillsboro.

Please clarify if Synopsis was included as an in-process development.
As discussed with City staff, the application for Synopsis has expired and was not included in this
analysis.

Needs to provide more detail on the proposed improvements at Shaleen and Cornelius
Pass Road and why they were chosen; why signalization was not a viable option.
Based on coordination with the City and projected traffic volumes at this intersection, signal
warrants are not met at this intersection. The northbound right-turn is proposed to improve access
into the site and reduce delay incurred by northbound through motorists. The northbound receiving
lane provides a two-stage movement for eastbound left-turning vehicles from Shaleen Street.
These improvements will help to reduce delay and potential conflicts at this intersection,
particularly for the eastbound approach.

The trip generation figures for the two 5,600 sf retail buildings appear to be low, especially
considering the potential for restaurants to occupy the space. Need to discuss appropriate
trip generation figures with City and County transportation staff.
Based on discussions with the applicant, it is estimated that up to approximately 30% of the outlot
space could be leased as a restaurant use and satisfy City parking codes. With the assumption of
the restaurant land use the outlot building area has been reduced to a total of 9,500 sf. Please see
PACLAND'S analysis of potential restaurant use in the project's response to the city's
completeness review.

Assuming 30 percent of the revised total outlot building area of 9,500 sf is restaurant use, an
updated trip generation analysis was completed assuming 2,850 sf of high turnover restaurant and
6,650 sf of retail space. Table 1 shows the resulting trip generation summary with a detailed trip
generation spreadsheets provided in Attachment 2. As a comparison, the trip generation from the
May 2013 TIA has also been provided.

As shown in the tables, with the reduction in overall retail space and the addition of the restaurant
land use the net new trip generation for the site remains the same during the weekday PM peak
hour and increases by 26 trips during the weekday AM peak hour. Based on the anticipated trip
generation figures no further analysis is necessary as increases during the AM peak hour are
minimal and are well within the site access driveway capacity.

Provide a sight distance study for the internal access points on Shaleen Loop.
The loop road will be constructed to meet City of Hillsboro public road standards. (PACLAND to
provide preliminary sight distance certification)

Address/analyze the potential for cut-through traffic on Shaleen Loop.
Based on a review of the site plan and projected operational conditions at the intersection of W
Baseline Road / SW Cornelius Pass Road it is not anticipated that a significant amount of motorist
will utilize the Shaleen Loop as a cut-through route. Elements supporting these findings include:
      Two potential travel routes would use this cut-through as an alternative to traveling
           through the W Baseline Road / SW Cornelius Pass Road intersection: (1) the westbound
           right-turn from W Baseline Road onto SW Cornelius Pass Road; and (2) the southbound
           left-turn from SW Cornelius Pass Road onto W Baseline Road.



                                                                                                                                     2
        The project is constructing a westbound right-turn lane at the intersection of W Baseline
        Road / SW Cornelius Pass Road and will improve travel time for motorist traveling
        westbound on W Baseline Road seeking to travel northbound on Cornelius Pass Road.
        Use of the internal roadway site roadway with a low design speed and through both
        commercial and residential accesses would likely not improve travel time.
        Vehicles traveling southbound on SW Cornelius Pass Road would be required to make
        two left-turn movements and travel through an internal site roadway with a low design
        speed and through both residential and commercial accesses. The southbound left-turn
        movement at W Baseline Road / SW Cornelius Pass Road is anticipated to operate at
        LOS C during the weekday PM peak hour (15 min). No travel time savings is anticipated
        through use of this cut-through route. Signal timing at the proposed signal on W Baseline
        Road can be timed to provide the majority of green time to Baseline road reducing the
        benefits obtained from this cut-through route.
        Based on intersection delay and travel time, no time savings is anticipated for cut-through
        vehicles. Detailed calculations are shown in Attachment 3.


Additional information
Update SPIS analysis utilizing crash reduction factors from ODOT. In addition, include a
SPIS analysis at the intersection of SW Cornelius Pass Road / NE Shaleen Street.
At the intersection of W Baseline Road / SW Cornelius Pass Road a westbound right-turn lane is
proposed with the project. Crash Reduction Factors (CRFs) obtained from the Update and
Enhancement of ODOT's Crash Reduction Factors (June 2006) were applied to specific crash
types prior to completing the benefit to cost analysis within the SPIS analysis. CRFs are utilized to
determine the effectiveness of an improvement based on the types of collisions occurring at the
intersection or approach of the proposed improvement.

Attachment 4 provides the specific reduction factors used for the improvement. A review of the
collision data show a total of 8 injury related collisions on the westbound approach. As shown in
Attachment 4, the CRF for a right-turn lane on a major road at a signalized intersection is 9% for
an injury related accident. The updated B/C ratio calculation is shown below:

         B/C = (Annual Benefits) * (Series Present Worth Factor (20 yrs @ 10%) / Estimated
         Improvement Cost

                 Annual Benefit = [(12 reported PDO Collisions) * 2 * $1,190 + (301 total
                 number of injuries) * $9,300 + (0 total number of fatalities) * $220,000]
                 / 3 = $102,520
                      o 1. CRF = (8 * (1 ­ 0.09) + (31 - 8) = 30 total number of injuries
                 Improvement Cost = Approximately $100,000
                 Present Worth Factor = 8.5136

         B/C = 8.73

The intersection of SW Cornelius Pass Road / NE Shaleen Street was also reviewed as it is within
the Washington County impact area and is identified on the SPIS list. A review of collisions within
the last three years shows that five collisions have occurred at this intersection. They include:
      Two rear end, one northbound and one southbound
      One fixed object due to reckless driving
      One turn due to a left-turning vehicle from Shaleen Street not yielding the ROW
      One angle due to driving and passing in the wrong lane

                                                 Attachment 4


3.1.3 Add right-turn lane on major road, signalized intersection
Main Category:                         Intersection
Character:                             Urban
Crash Types Addressed:                 Angle, Rear-End, Sideswipe ­ Overtaking, Turning
Other Causes:                          Turning Volumes, Congestion




                           Figure 3.3: Right-turn lane on major road, signalized intersection



Summary discussion:
Providing right-turn lanes at signalized intersections can reduce collisions between right-turning
and following through vehicles, particularly on high-volume and high-speed roads. However, it
is important to note that the installation of right-turn lanes at signalized intersections carries the
potential to create other safety and/or operational problems such as vehicles in right-turn lanes
blocking cross-street driver's line of sight, and decreased distance to roadside objects if
installation of right-turn lanes was accomplished by shoulder re-striping. Sufficient guidance
through the intersection is an important consideration with exclusive right-turn lanes. In some
instances, channelization may be desirable. In addition, raised islands can serve as a refuge for
pedestrians, an important consideration when right-turn lanes result in increased crossing
distances and pedestrian exposure to traffic. These CRFs apply to one approach.

     Table 3.5: Right-turn lane on major road, signalized intersection recommended CRFs*
     Character      Crash Type             Fatal        Injury        PDO        All Crashes
     Urban          All Crash Types        9%           9%            -          4%
    * for 4-leg intersections only



Reviewed study title:
Harwood, D.W., K.M. Bauer, I.B. Potts, D.J. Torbic, K.R. Richard, E.R. Kohlman Rabbani,
E. Hauer, and L. Elefteriadou. Safety Effectiveness of Intersection Left- and Right-Turn Lanes.
Federal Highway Administration. McLean, VA. 2002.

                                 Executive Summary
Description and Locations. The proposed mixed use residential/retail project is located on
the northeast corner of the W Baseline Road/Cornelius Pass Road intersection in the City of
Hillsboro. The project includes the development of up to 250 apartment units along with a
50,000 sf grocery store and 11,200 sf of general retail space.

Access to the site is proposed via a new public roadway that connects from an access point
on SW Cornelius Pass Road opposite NE Shaleen Street to an access point on W Baseline
Road at SW 215th Avenue. No vehicular access to the residential neighborhoods east or
north of the site is proposed due to restrictions imposed on the site development via City
ordinance. Non-motorized connections will be maintained however to provide access for
pedestrians. The new public roadway intersection with Cornelius Pass Road is proposed to
be restricted to three-quarter access, with left-turns out of the site restricted. In addition a
northbound right-turn lane at this intersection is proposed to facilitate travel into the site.

A traffic signal is proposed at the W Baseline Road access point. This access point would
align with SW 215th Avenue. The analysis shows that a signal is warranted at this location.
The development is also proposing to install a westbound right-turn lane at the intersection of
W Baseline Road/Cornelius Pass Road intersection.

Analysis Scope. The scope of the analysis focused on the weekday mid-day and PM peak
hour period and included those intersections within the influence and impact areas as defined
by the City of Hillsboro and Washington County land use code. The scope of the analysis,
including key assumptions, was approved by City of Hillsboro and Washington County staff
during the scoping process. The study area was defined based on standards for projects
within 2,600 feet of a station community and resulted in a study area with 26 intersections. In
addition to a mid-day and PM peak hour analysis, an AM analysis at the site access
intersections and the intersection of SW Cornelius Pass Road / W Baseline Road was also
completed, although not specifically mandated by City of Hillsboro or Washington County
code.

Key Methodologies. The project is anticipated to be completed by 2015, and as such was
identified for the analysis horizon year. The analysis included a review of intersection
performance including intersection level of service (LOS) and vehicle queuing near the site.
The LOS analysis was completed using Synchro software and the queuing analysis was
completed using VISSIM. VISSIM is a micro-simulation model that simulates vehicle and
pedestrian flows, factoring in the storage pockets to be provided at the proposed access
points, travel patterns and lane change selection characteristics, and any coordination and
interaction with existing and proposed traffic signals.

Trip Generation. Trip rates used as a basis for estimating the trip generation for the project
was based on ITE Trip Generation, 9th Edition. The proposed project is anticipated to
generate 4,609 net new weekday daily trips, with 430 net new trips occurring during the
weekday PM peak hour trip and 307 trips occurring during the weekday AM peak hour. To
verify the applicability of ITE trip rates for the Supermarket element of the project, site specific
trip generation studies were done at four Neighborhood Market stores. Additional information
on this study is included in the Trip Generation section of this report. This study showed that
ITE trip rates are approximately 60% higher than the weighted average trip rates observed at
the Neighborhood Market stores.

Analysis Results. As noted in the description of the scope of work, a total of four time
periods were evaluated within this study.




                                                                                              Page ii
Transportation Impact Analysis
Sequoia Village                                                                        May 2013


        Weekday Mid-Day Peak Hour (One Hour). All study intersections would operate at
        LOS C or better during the 2015 with-project weekday mid-day peak hour.

        Weekday PM Peak Hour (One Hour). All study intersections would operate at LOS D
        or better during the 2015 with-project weekday PM peak hour.

        Weekday PM Peak Hour (15-Min). All study intersections would operate at LOS D or
        better during the 2015 with-project weekday PM peak 15 minute period.

        Weekday AM Peak Hour (15-Min). All study intersections would operate at LOS C or
        better during the 2015 with-project weekday AM peak 15 minute period.

A VISSIM simulation model was developed to evaluate the future queuing at the site access
and adjacent intersections along W Baseline Road and Cornelius Pass Road SW. The model
included the intersections along Cornelius Pass Road from Samantha Lane to W Baseline
Road and along W Baseline Road from Promenade to SW 215th Avenue. The analysis
showed that under 2015 without-project conditions, two movements are forecast to have
queues (95th percentile) that extend beyond existing storage lengths. These include the
northbound left-turn queue at the intersection of W Baseline Road / SW Cornelius Pass Road
which is forecast to exceed the available storage by approximately two vehicles and the
northbound queue at the intersection of W Baseline Road / Promenade which is forecast to
exceed the storage by approximately one vehicle. With the improvements proposed and the
resulting optimization of the W Baseline Road and Cornelius Pass Road intersection, no
increase in these two movements are forecast. In addition, all other vehicle queues at the
intersections evaluated in this VISSIM model are anticipated to be accommodated within the
existing storage.

Proposed Mitigation. The project has included the construction of a westbound right-turn
lane at the W Baseline Road / SW Cornelius Pass Road intersection. This improvements
provides additional intersection capacity, improving overall intersection performance. The
additional intersection capacity and improvement in intersection congestion addresses the
traffic safety related impacts identified through a review of the Washington County SPIS list.
Based on the formula and standards developed by Washington County, the construction of a
westbound right-turn lane would satisfy and mitigate for impacts to this critical intersection.

Transportation Impact Analysis
Sequoia Village                                                                          May 2013


                                    Introduction
This Transportation Impact Analysis (TIA) summarizes the potential transportation-related
impacts associated with the proposed Sequoia Village development located in the City of
Hillsboro. The analysis was conducted to evaluate the project's impacts on roadways and
intersections within the vicinity of the site and to recommend, if necessary, mitigation
measures that would reduce or otherwise offset these impacts. The scope of the analysis
was prepared in coordination with both the City of Hillsboro and Washington County staff.

Project Description
The project site is located on the northeast corner of the SW Cornelius Pass Road/
W Baseline Road intersection in the City of Hillsboro, Oregon. The site vicinity is shown in
Figure 1.

The project would construct up to 50,000 sf of grocery store use, 11,200 sf of general retail,
and 250 residential units. A preliminary site plan is shown in Figure 2. Access to the site
would be provided through a new public roadway that intersects with SW Cornelius Pass
road opposite NE Shaleen Street to W Baseline Road at SW 215th Avenue. The intersection
with SW Cornelius Pass Road would be would be reconfigured to allow three-quarter1 access
to/from the site and full access from the west leg while full access movements from
W Baseline Road is proposed via the installation of a traffic signal. Although non-motorized
connections would be provided to the neighborhood north and east of the site through a City
of Hillsboro ordinance, vehicle connections are restricted. The project is expected to be
completed and occupied by 2015.

Analysis Approach and Study Area
The scope of this analysis was prepared through coordination and direction from the City of
Hillsboro and Washington County staff and reviewing their respective road and intersection
standard requirements. The sections below discuss the off-site and site access analysis
approach used within this study.


Off-Site Analysis Approach
Washington County Code identifies the influence area for a project to be any roadway
segment/intersection where the daily impact of the proposed project is more than 10 percent
of the existing Average Weekday Daily Traffic (AWDT) (dual direction) on the roadway
network or within 600 feet of the property line. This is known as the 10 percent rule. Figure 3
illustrates the projects impact on the adjacent roadway. As shown in Figure 3, the project
dissipates to less than 10 percent within 1,000 feet of the project.

City of Hillsboro Land Use Code (Section 137.XVI.C) states that developments within 2,600
feet of an LRT station are considered to be within a station community. The traffic analysis
report shall analyze the impact of the project on the City, County and State road and street
systems within one mile of the development or to such a greater distance as necessary until
the traffic analysis shows that the impact of the project or phase of a project has dissipated to
less than 10 percent. As shown in Figure 3, the project dissipates to less than 10 percent
within approximately ¼ mile of the project. Therefore, intersections within one mile of the
development were reviewed. Based on coordination and direction from City staff the following
intersections were identified for analysis:




1
    Left-in/right-in/right-out

    26.   SE Frances St / SE Century Blvd                 (Unsignalized)

As identified in the Hillsboro code, intersections within one mile need to be studied during the
weekday mid-day (12:00 PM to 2:00 PM) and the weekday "peak" hour. The City does not
specifically identify the "peak" hour to be studied. Based on a review of AM, mid-day, and PM
traffic counts near the site as well as consideration of site generated traffic, the weekday PM
peak hour (4:00 PM to 6:00 PM) was considered as this time period represents the highest
background and project generated traffic volumes.

The weekday PM peak hour is studied for both the one hour peak and the 20-minute peak
between 4:00 PM and 6:00 PM. For the weekday PM peak hour, the 15-minute peak hour
factors were used in place of the 20-minute peak. This results in a higher peaking
characteristic by concentrating the peak traffic flow period throughout the hour in a smaller
time duration. This results in a more conservative analysis.


Access Analysis Approach
LOS was evaluated at the access driveways during the weekday AM, mid-day, and PM peak
hour. Although not required, the weekday AM was also evaluated to document the
anticipated impacts at the site access points as well as the intersection of SW Cornelius Pass
Road / W Baseline Road.

In addition to intersection LOS analysis, a queuing analysis was completed using VISSIM
simulation model software package. VISSIM is a micro-simulation model that simulates
vehicle and pedestrian flows, factoring in the storage pockets to be provided at the proposed
access points, travel patterns and lane change selection characteristics, and any coordination
and interaction with existing and proposed traffic signals. The weekday PM peak hour was
chosen as it exhibits the highest congestion of traffic on adjacent roadways to/from the site
throughout the day.

 Existing and Future Without-Project Conditions
This section describes both existing conditions and 2015 without-project conditions within the
identified study area. Study area characteristics are provided for the roadway network,
planned improvements, existing and forecasted without-project volumes, traffic operations,
and non-motorized facilities. Future without-project conditions reported in this section provide
a basis for measuring future traffic impacts associated with the proposal.


Roadway Network
The street system within the project vicinity includes two-way streets, generally including non-
motorized facilities for both pedestrians and bicyclists. Table 1 describes the existing
roadway characteristics in the proposed project vicinity. In general, the roadway descriptions
given apply to the portions of the roadways within the study area of the proposed project.

Non-Motorized Facilities
Sidewalks are provided along most all of the nearby streets with crosswalks located adjacent
to the site at the SW Cornelius Pass Road / W Baseline Road. Crosswalks are also provided
at other major junctions along SW Cornelius Pass Road and W Baseline Road including
intersections with SW 205th Avenue, SW 197th Avenue, NW 231st Avenue, and SW Augusta
Lane. Bike lanes exist along SW Cornelius Pass Road, W Baseline Road, and other road

                                                                                                     Page 9
Transportation Impact Analysis
Sequoia Village                                                                         May 2013


collectors as seen in Table 1. Other roadways within the study area may provide paved
shoulders wide enough to accommodate bicycles but do not explicitly identify these facilities
for bicycle use. No near or long-term future construction of dedicated bike lanes is anticipated
within the study area as identified in the Hillsboro Transportation System Plan Update (2004).


Planned Improvements
The City of Hillsboro Capital Improvement Projects List and the Washington County Capital
Projects list were reviewed to identify any planned improvements within the 2015 horizon
year. No capacity improvements within the study area were identified within either plan.
However, a traffic signal will be constructed at the W Baseline Road/SW 201st Avenue
intersection as mitigation for an in-process development project approved by the County.


Traffic Volumes
Weekday mid-day and PM peak hour traffic volumes at the study intersection were collected
in June 2012 and March 2013 while local schools were in session. Although SW Cornelius
Pass Road has been under construction during several periods over the last year, the
roadway was open to traffic during the periods when turning movement counts were being
performed. The existing weekday mid-day and PM peak hour traffic volumes are illustrated in
Figure 4 and Figure 5. Detailed traffic count worksheets are provided in Appendix A. A
detailed discussion regarding the weekday AM peak hour is included in the site access
analysis section.

Utilizing the Metro regional travel demand models (2010 vs 2035) a two percent annual
growth rate was identified and determined appropriate for forecasting future traffic volumes
within the study area through coordination with City of Hillsboro and County staff. In addition
to an annual growth rate, eight development projects that are approved, but not yet
constructed ("pipeline" projects) were included in the 2015 without-project weekday PM peak
hour traffic volumes. These include:
         Living Green at Orenco
         Holland Wrap
         Orchards at Orenco
         Intel RAP2
         Intel Ronler Acres
         Alma Gardens
         Residential project on northeast corner of Baseline / SW 201st Avenue
         Residential project on southeast corner of Cornelius Pass Road / Baseline Road

Information for each of the projects was provided by City of Hillsboro and Washington County
staff. Figure 6 and Figure 7 illustrate the resulting 2015 without-project weekday mid-day and
PM peak hour traffic volumes.

Traffic Operations
A level of service (LOS) analysis was conducted for the study area intersections for the
weekday AM, mid-day, and PM peak period. As noted previously, the results for the weekday
AM peak hour analysis are summarized in the site access section of this report. Existing and
future without-project levels of service, delays, and volume-to-capacity (v/c) ratios were
calculated at study intersections based on the methodologies contained in the Highway
Capacity Manual. The software program Synchro 8 was used to evaluate intersection
operations. Based on coordination with City and County staff HCM 2000 methodologies were
used for both the unsignalized and signalized intersection analysis.

LOS values range from LOS A, which indicates good operating conditions with little or no
delay, to LOS F, which indicates extreme congestion and long vehicle delays. LOS is
measured in terms of total average intersection delay for signalized and all-way stop-
controlled intersections. A more detailed explanation of the LOS criteria is provided in
Appendix B.

Performance and operational standards applied to the study area intersections are outlined in
Table 2 for both Washington County and City of Hillsboro.

Table 2.         Intersection Performance Standards
Jurisdiction                  Traffic Control       Standard

                        1      Unsignalized /
Washington County                                   Intersection v/c  0.99
                                Signalized
                                                    Critical Regional Facilities (SW Cornelius Pass Road)
                                                    Mid-day standard (one-hour) ­ LOS D
                                                                              3
                                                    Peak one hour standard (one-hour) ­ LOS E
                                                                                        4
                                                    Peak one hour standard (20-minute ) ­ LOS E
                    2          Unsignalized /
City of Hillsboro
                                Signalized
                                                    Other Facilities
                                                    Mid-day standard (one hour) ­ LOS D
                                                    Peak one hour standard (one hour) ­LOS D
                                                                                      4
                                                    Peak one hour standard (20-minute ) ­LOS E
1.   Washington County Transportation Plan (3/31/2003), Table 5.
2.   City of Hillsboro land use code (Section 137.XVI.C), Table 137.4.
3.   The peak hour standard occurs during the weekday PM peak hour.
4.   As discussed in the study approach, the 15-minute peak was evaluated, resulting in a conservative analysis.


Based on coordination with City and County staff, the evaluation of unsignalized intersections
was completed using the weighted average control delay of stop controlled approaches.
Although the standard is based on the overall weighted average, the worst movement is also
reported. Signalized intersections were evaluated using signal timing information provided by
Washington County and City of Hillsboro staff. Where a center two-way left-turn lane exists
and supported by field observations, two-stage gap acceptance methodology was applied to
unsignalized intersections based on discussions with City and County staff.

As stated in Table 137.4 of the Hillsboro land use code a one hour analysis for the peak mid-
day peak hour and a one hour and 20-minute peak analysis for the weekday peak hour is
required. A 15-minute peak was used in place of the 20-minute peak, resulting in a
conservative analysis. Table 3 and Table 4 show the existing weekday mid-day and PM peak
hour LOS. LOS worksheets are provided in Appendix C.

As shown in Table 3, all study intersections currently operate at LOS C or better during the
weekday mid-day peak hour. Table 4 shows that during the weekday PM peak one-hour and
15-minute time periods all study intersections are anticipated to operate at LOS C or better
with the exception of W Baseline Road / SW 201st Avenue, which operates at LOS F during

                                                                                                                    Page 15
Transportation Impact Analysis
Sequoia Village                                                                                                        May 2013


both time periods. The LOS deficiency for this unsignalized intersection is due to the limited
number of gaps for minor street movements from W Baseline Road. Based on the LOS
standards shown in Table 2, W Baseline Road / SW 201st Avenue is below the City of
Hillsboro standard during the one hour and 15-minute time periods.

Tables 5 through Table 7 summarize 2015 baseline traffic operations. The existing conditions
LOS are also shown in each table as a comparison. The signal timings were optimized for the
future without-project conditions, accounting for change in traffic attributed to background
growth and pipeline projects.

Weekday Mid-Day Peak Hour (One Hour). As shown in Table 5, all study intersections
would operate at LOS C or better under the baseline 2015 conditions. Overall intersection
LOS and V/C ratio measurements (overall and movement specific) operate within City and
County standards.

Weekday PM Peak Hour (One Hour). As shown in Table 6, during the weekday PM peak
one-hour time period all study intersections are anticipated to operate at LOS C or better.
With signalization of W Baseline Road / SW 201st Avenue intersection LOS will improve from
LOS F in existing conditions to LOS B in 2015 without project conditions.

Weekday PM Peak Hour (15-Min). As shown in Table 7, during the weekday PM peak 15-
minute time period all study intersections are anticipated to operate at LOS D or better. With
the construction of the Baseline Road / SW 201st Avenue signal, the LOS will improve from
LOS F in existing conditions to LOS B in 2015 without project conditions.

Traffic Safety
Collision records were reviewed within the study area to identify any potential traffic safety
issues. The most recent summary of collision data from ODOT is for the three-year period
between January 1, 2009 and December 31, 2011. A historical review of the frequency of
collisions was conducted at study intersections. Collisions per million entering vehicles (MEV)
was also calculated; typically locations with more than one collisions per MEV should be

As shown in Table 8, several of the study area intersections have had zero collisions reported
over the three-year analysis period. At those intersections where collisions have been

reported, the average number ranged between approximately 0.8 and 8.67 collisions per
year. The highest number of annual collisions occurred at the intersection of W Baseline
Road / Cornelius Pass Road. Further analysis of this intersection was conducted and is
summarized in the following paragraphs.

In addition to the collision data summary in Table 8, a traffic safety analysis was completed
based on Washington County guidelines and data provided by the Oregon Department of
Transportation (ODOT) to determine if any traffic safety improvements are necessary within
the study area. The impact area is defined by roadways where the site generated traffic
exceeds 10 percent and intersections identified within the top 100 intersections within the
County SPIS (Safety Priority Index System) list. Based on these criteria, the intersection of
Cornelius Pass Road / W Baseline Road was studied as it is listed as number 68 on the
current Washington County SPIS list. Collision data from 2006 to 2011 provided by Oregon
Department of Transportation (ODOT) and is summarized in Table 9. Intersection
improvements at this location were completed in 2005, improving capacity at all approaches
to the intersection.

1. Higher number of crashes reported in 2011 compared to previous years due to a change to an internal process that allows the

As shown in Table 9, collisions at the intersection of W Baseline Road / Cornelius Pass Road
total approximately eight per year with 0.51 collisions per MEV. The most frequent collision
type was rear end and turn related collisions. No fatalities occurred during the study period.

Per Washington County requirements, a benefit-cost analysis was completed to determine if
a road improvement is necessary based on the collision history at the intersection. A benefit
to cost analysis of the collisions compared to a potential capacity improvement was
completed using guidelines outlined in the Determining Traffic Safety Improvements Under
The Traffic Impact Fee Ordinance (July 1986). As discussed in this document, if the benefit-
cost ratio is less than 1.0, no improvements are required to offset the impacts of collisions.

One potential improvement (which is being proposed) is the implementation of a westbound
right-turn lane. The benefit to cost ratio was calculated using the following formula, based on
the previous three years of accident data:

            B/C = (Annual Benefits / 3)*(Series Present Worth Factor (20 yrs @ 10%) /
            Estimated Improvement Cost

                   Annual Benefit = $105,620 (Collisions included 12 Property
                    Damage Only and 31 injury)
                   Improvement Cost = Approximately $100,000
                   Present Worth Factor = 8.5136

            B/C = 8.99

Based on the Benefit-cost ratio greater than 1.0, the identified improvement is warranted.

                                       Project Impacts
This section of the report documents the site-generated impacts of the proposed project on
the surrounding roadway network, including impacts to traffic volumes and intersection
operations. Project-generated weekday AM, mid-day, and PM peak hour traffic volumes are
estimated, distributed, and assigned to the surrounding roadway network. Future with-project
traffic volumes are projected and intersection peak hour operations are evaluated. 2015
without- and with-project conditions are compared in order to identify transportation impacts
associated with the project.


Trip Generation
Trip generation estimates for the project were developed using rates identified in the ITE Trip
Generation Manual, 9th Edition. The trip generation estimate is based on a Grocery Store
(LU 850) for a store size of approximately 50,000 gsf, Shopping Center (LU 820) totaling
approximately 11,200 gsf, and a residential apartment complex (LU 220) totaling
approximately 250 units. Based on the mix of land uses, the site would experience both
internal and pass-by trips.

With the interaction of the grocery store along with the retail outlots and residential land uses,
it is anticipated that there will be a number of trips that occur internal to the site. These trips
are referred to as internal trips. The ITE Trip Generation Handbook contains information
related to potential internalization between uses. ITE also has developed a procedure for
estimating the number of trips that occur internal to the site given the directional trip
generation and assumed percentages. Based on discussions with County and City staff, the
internal trip reduction for the residential uses was capped at 15 percent of the residential
trips. Based on the assumptions, the overall internal trip reduction for the site is anticipated to
be approximately 10 percent of the overall trip generation.

Pass-by trips represent trips that are currently passing by the site. With the addition of the
proposed development, these trips would stop at the site before continuing on their way. As
such, the trips do not represent new trips to the adjacent roadway system.

To verify the trip rates for the grocery store use an independent study of four neighborhood
market locations was completed during the weekday mid-day and PM peak hour for two
consecutive days in April and May 2013. Although the proposed grocery store use is
consistent with ITE land use description, additional verification of the trip rates used in this
analysis was completed. The location and characteristics of each study location are identified
in Table 10. A detailed trip generation summary for each site and day is included in
Appendix E.

Table 10. Study Location Characteristics and Trip Rate Summary

                                                         Weighted Average        Weighted Average

the weekday mid-day peak hour and 5.82 trips per ksf during the weekday PM peak hour.

ITE trip rates in the analysis is considered conservative.

The proposed development is calculated to generate a total of 4,609 net new weekday daily
trips, with 430 net new trips occurring during the weekday PM peak hour trip and 307 trips
occurring during the weekday AM peak hour. The mid-day analysis was completed assuming
trip generation generated for the weekday PM peak hour. As noted above, these calculations
are based on national historic information and are substantially higher than locally collected
comparable data. The use of a ITE rates represents a worst case approach to characterizing
future conditions.


Trip Distribution
The distribution patterns for project traffic was developed for both residential and retail land
uses using separate distributions. The residential land use distribution was based on the a
select zone assignment for a residential zone3 using the Metro Regional Travel Demand
Model and distribution patterns observed through turning movement counts. The retail land
use distribution was completed using the regional model4, turning movement counts, existing
trip distribution patterns observed at the retail center located on the southwest corner of W
Baseline Road / SW Cornelius Pass Road, and consideration of other grocery stores in the
vicinity of the site. It should be noted that there are five grocery stores located within three
miles of the site. The resulting distribution for the weekday mid-day and PM peak hour are

   Pass Road / W Baseline Road, was used.

Traffic Operations
A level of service analysis was conducted for the study area intersections for the analysis
periods discussed previously. As part of the proposed development plan, several
improvements to the adjacent intersections (shown in Figure 2) have been assumed. These
include:
      Signalization of the intersection of W Baseline Road / 215th Avenue SW and addition
         of a north leg of the intersection (site access).
      The addition of a westbound right-turn lane at the intersection of W Baseline Road /
         SW Cornelius Pass Road.
      Addition of a westbound leg at the intersection of SW Cornelius Pass Road / NE
         Shaleen Street providing access to the development. This intersection will provide full
         access for the existing eastbound approach with an eastbound left refuge lane. The
         westbound approach will be restricted to right-in/right-out/left-in movements only.

Signal timing settings for the with-project analysis were consistent with the without project
analysis, with the exception of the new signalized access at W Baseline Road / SW 215th
Avenue and the adjacent coordinated signals to the west including W Baseline Road / SW
Cornelius Pass Road, W Baseline Road / Promenade access, and W Baseline Road / SW
Borwick Street.

The results of the mid-day one hour and PM peak one hour and 15-min peak LOS analysis
are summarized in Table 12, Table 13, and Table 14. The results of the 2015 without-project
analyses have also been included as a comparison. Levels of service worksheets for 2015
with-project traffic conditions are included in Appendix C of this report.

Weekday Mid-Day Peak Hour (One Hour). As shown in Table 12, all study intersections
would operate at LOS C or better during the 2015 with-project weekday mid-day peak hour.

Weekday PM Peak Hour (One Hour). As shown in Table 13 during the weekday PM peak
one-hour time period all study intersections would operate at LOS D or better. As noted in the
table, the delay at W Baseline Road / SW 211th Avenue improves from without project
conditions to with-project conditions. The reduction in average delay is due to the weighted
average delay calculations and additional traffic assigned to a lower delay movement.

Weekday PM Peak Hour (15-Min). As shown in Table 14 the weekday PM peak 15-minute
time period all study intersections are anticipated to operate at LOS D or better. Consistent
with the PM peak one hour, the delay improves from without to with-project conditions. This is
due to the additional southbound right-turns at the intersection reducing the overall
intersection delay.

Site Access Analysis
This section discusses the traffic operations, signal warrant analysis, and vehicle queuing
analysis completed at the site access points and adjacent intersections. The purpose of this
analysis is to verify that the proposed access points will operate adequately.

Washington County intersection spacing standards require 600 feet spacing between
intersections (stop bar to stop bar). As described previously, the project proposes to construct
a fourth leg to the W Baseline Road/SW 215th Avenue intersection and the SW Cornelius
Pass Road/NE Shaleen Street intersection. Neither one of these intersections currently meet

                                                                                                                        Page 36
Transportation Impact Analysis
Sequoia Village                                                                            May 2013


the County's spacing standards. However, the access points have been aligned with these
existing intersections based on discussions with City and County staff and the desire to avoid
the creation of multiple offset intersections. An Access Modification Request will be
processed through Washington County as part of the access approval process.

Sight distance at the proposed W Baseline Road and SW Cornelius Pass Road access points
was reviewed in the field. The proposed site driveways are aligned with existing streets
opposite the site. Sight distance in both travel directions was determined to not be
constrained by any horizontal or vertical obstructions. Sight triangles at the access points will
be maintained through review of future placement of the shops buildings and appropriate
identification of landscaping elements as to not block horizontal sight lines.


Site Access Level of Service
During the weekday mid-day peak hour the site access intersections are anticipated to
operate at LOS B or better. During the weekday PM peak one hour and 15-minute time
periods, W Baseline Road / SW 215th Avenue is anticipated to operate at LOS B and SW
Cornelius Pass Road / NE Shaleen Street is anticipated to operate at LOS D. The eastbound
approach is anticipated to operate at LOS F with approximately 53 seconds of delay during
the 15-minute peak and LOS E with approximately 41 seconds of delay during the one hour
peak. The weighted average control delay for the intersection is LOS D and is within the City
of Hillsboro standards.

As noted in the study approach an additional analysis was completed during the weekday AM
peak hour. Analysis of the weekday AM peak hour is not a requirement of the City or County
TIA standards, but has been provided to assess the project impacts at the site access
driveways and the intersection of SW Cornelius Pass Road / W Baseline Road. Traffic counts
for the weekday AM peak hour analysis were provided by the City of Hillsboro at the
intersection of W Baseline Road / SW Cornelius Pass Road. Additional counts were collected
at the intersection of SW Cornelius Pass Road / NE Shaleen Street and W Baseline Road /
SW 215th Avenue to determine the volume of traffic at the minor street approach for each
intersection.

The counts show that in general, traffic volumes during the weekday AM peak hour are
approximately 30 percent less than traffic volumes observed during the weekday PM peak
hour. In addition, as shown in Table 11, trip generation for the site is approximately 30
percent less during the weekday AM peak hour as compared to the weekday PM peak hour.
Figure 14 illustrates the 2015 with-project trip assignment and with-project traffic volumes
during the weekday AM peak hour.

The LOS analysis shows that all intersections are anticipated to operate at LOS C or better
during the weekday AM peak 15-minute time period. LOS worksheets are provided in
Appendix C.


Queuing Analysis
A queuing analysis was completed using the VISSIM simulation model software package to
understand the vehicle queues at the adjacent study intersections during the Weekday PM
peak hour. VISSIM is a microscopic traffic simulation model used to model urban traffic
operations and travel modes. VISSIM has the capability to analyze traffic, transit, and non-
motorized operations under many different geometric and operational constraints, such as
different lane configurations, traffic compositions, coordinated traffic signal corridors, transit
routes, and pedestrian crossings. VISSIM is used to estimate corridor operations and safety
of future planned development and street system design alternatives. In this application,
VISSIM is able to better evaluate the sensitivities associated with the impact of the traffic
signal at Cornelius Pass Road SW and SW Baseline Road on the planned project access
